style="text-align:center;background:lavender">Military service</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Rank</th><td><a href="/wiki/Admiral" title="Admiral">Admiral</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocean_Sea" title="Ocean Sea">Ocean Sea</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Christopher Columbus</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[a]</a></sup> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">k</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#652;/: \'u\' in \'cut\'">&#652;</span><span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">m</span><span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">b</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup> before 31 October 1451&#160;&#8211; 20 May 1506) was an <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a> explorer, navigator, and <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonist</a> who completed <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">four voyages</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a> of Spain. He led the first European expeditions to the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, initiating the permanent <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a>. Columbus discovered the viable sailing route to the Americas, a continent which was not then known to the <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">Old World</a>. While what he thought he had discovered was a route to the Far East, he is credited with the opening of the Americas for conquest and settlement by Europeans.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Origin_theories_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Origin theories of Christopher Columbus">Columbus\'s early life</a> is somewhat obscure, but scholars generally agree that he was born in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a> and spoke a dialect of <a href="/wiki/Ligurian_(Romance_language)" title="Ligurian (Romance language)">Ligurian</a> as his first language. He went to sea at a young age and travelled widely, as far north as the British Isles (and possibly Iceland) and as far south as what is now <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>. He married a Portuguese woman and was based in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> for several years, but later took a Spanish mistress; he had one son with each woman. Though largely self-educated, Columbus was widely read in geography, astronomy, and history. He formulated a plan to seek a western sea passage to the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>, hoping to profit from the lucrative <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a>.\n</p><p>After years of lobbying, the Catholic Monarchs of Spain <a href="/wiki/Capitulations_of_Santa_Fe" title="Capitulations of Santa Fe">agreed</a> to sponsor a journey west, in the name of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>. Columbus left Spain in August 1492 with three ships, and after a stopover in the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> made landfall in the Americas on 12 October (now celebrated as <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Day" title="Columbus Day">Columbus Day</a>). His landing place was an island in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, known by its native inhabitants as <a href="/wiki/Guanahani" title="Guanahani">Guanahani</a>; its exact location is uncertain. Columbus subsequently visited <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, establishing <a href="/wiki/La_Navidad" title="La Navidad">a colony</a> in what is now <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>&#8212;the first European settlement in the Americas since the <a href="/wiki/Norse_colonization_of_North_America" title="Norse colonization of North America">Norse colonies</a> almost 500 years earlier. He arrived back in Spain in early 1493, bringing a number of captive natives with him. <a href="/wiki/Columbus%27s_letter_on_the_first_voyage" title="Columbus\'s letter on the first voyage">Word of his discoveries</a> soon spread throughout Europe.\n</p><p>Columbus would make three further voyages to the New World, exploring the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> in 1493, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> and the northern coast of South America in 1498, and the eastern coast of Central America in 1502. Many of the names he gave to geographical features&#8212;particularly islands&#8212;are still in use. He continued to seek a passage to the East Indies, and the extent to which he was aware that the Americas were a wholly separate landmass is uncertain; he gave the name <i>indios</i> ("Indians") to the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples</a> he encountered. Columbus\'s strained relationship with the Spanish crown and its appointed colonial administrators in America led to his arrest and removal from Hispaniola in 1500, and later to <a href="/wiki/Pleitos_colombinos" title="Pleitos colombinos">protracted litigation</a> over the benefits that he and his heirs claimed were owed to them by the crown.\n</p><p>Columbus\'s expeditions inaugurated a period of exploration, conquest, and colonization that lasted for centuries, helping create the modern <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a>. The transfers between the <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">Old World</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> that followed his first voyage are known as the <a href="/wiki/Columbian_exchange" title="Columbian exchange">Columbian exchange</a>, and the period of human habitation in the Americas prior to his arrival is known as the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian era</a>. Columbus\'s legacy continues to be debated. He was widely venerated in the centuries after his death, but public perceptions have changed as recent scholars have given attention to negative aspects of his life, such as his role in the extinction of the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta&#237;no">Ta&#237;no</a> people, his promotion of slavery, and allegations of tyranny towards Spanish colonists. Many landmarks and institutions in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a> bear his name, including the country of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" considerations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Nautical_considerations"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Nautical considerations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Quest_for_financial_support_for_a_voyage"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Quest for financial support for a voyage</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Agreement_with_the_Spanish_crown"><span class="tocnumber">2.5</span> <span class="toctext">Agreement with the Spanish crown</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Voyages"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Voyages</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#First_voyage"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">First voyage</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Second_voyage"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Second voyage</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Third_voyage"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Third voyage</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Fourth_voyage"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Fourth voyage</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Accusations_of_tyranny"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Accusations of tyranny</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Later_life"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Later life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Illness_and_death"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Illness and death</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Commemoration"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Commemoration</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Legacy"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Legacy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Discoverer"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Discoverer</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Flat_Earth_mythology"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Flat Earth mythology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#America_as_a_distinct_land"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">America as a distinct land</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Criticism_and_defense_in_modern_scholarship"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">Criticism and defense in modern scholarship</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#Slavery_and_serfdom"><span class="tocnumber">8.4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Slavery and serfdom</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-23"><a href="#Violence_towards_Natives_and_Spanish_colonists"><span class="tocnumber">8.4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Violence towards Natives and Spanish colonists</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-24"><a href="#Black_Legend"><span class="tocnumber">8.4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Black Legend</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Physical_appearance"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Physical appearance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information on Columbus\'s birthplace and family background: <a href="/wiki/Origin_theories_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Origin theories of Christopher Columbus">Origin theories of Christopher Columbus</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Christopher_Columbus_at_the_gates_of_the_monastery_of_Santa_Maria_de_la_Rabida_with_his_son_Diego.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2881" data-file-width="2113" decoding="async" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Christopher_Columbus_at_the_gates_of_the_monastery_of_Santa_Maria_de_la_Rabida_with_his_son_Diego.jpg/170px-Christopher_Columbus_at_the_gates_of_the_monastery_of_Santa_Maria_de_la_Rabida_with_his_son_Diego.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Christopher_Columbus_at_the_gates_of_the_monastery_of_Santa_Maria_de_la_Rabida_with_his_son_Diego.jpg/255px-Christopher_Columbus_at_the_gates_of_the_monastery_of_Santa_Maria_de_la_Rabida_with_his_son_Diego.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Christopher_Columbus_at_the_gates_of_the_monastery_of_Santa_Maria_de_la_Rabida_with_his_son_Diego.jpg/340px-Christopher_Columbus_at_the_gates_of_the_monastery_of_Santa_Maria_de_la_Rabida_with_his_son_Diego.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Christopher_Columbus_at_the_gates_of_the_monastery_of_Santa_Maria_de_la_Rabida_with_his_son_Diego.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Christopher Columbus at the gates of the <a href="/wiki/La_R%C3%A1bida_Friary" title="La R&#225;bida Friary">monastery of Santa Mar&#237;a de la R&#225;bida</a> with his son Diego</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Benet_Mercad%C3%A9" title="Benet Mercad&#233;">Benet Mercad&#233;</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The name <i>Christopher Columbus</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Anglicisation" title="Anglicisation">Anglicisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <b>Christophorus Columbus</b>. His name in <a href="/wiki/Ligurian_(Romance_language)" title="Ligurian (Romance language)">Ligurian</a> is  <b>Crist&#242;ffa C&#243;mbo</b>, in <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> <b>Cristoforo Colombo</b> and in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> <b>Crist&#243;bal Col&#243;n</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeazley1911741_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeazley1911741-5">[4]</a></sup> He was born before 31 October 1451 in the territory of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a> (now part of modern Italy), though the exact location remains disputed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips19929_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips19929-6">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[b]</a></sup> His father was <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Colombo" title="Domenico Colombo">Domenico Colombo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeazley1911741_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeazley1911741-5">[4]</a></sup> a middle-class wool weaver who worked both in <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Savona" title="Savona">Savona</a> and who also owned a cheese stand at which young Christopher worked as a helper. His mother was <a href="/wiki/Susanna_Fontanarossa" title="Susanna Fontanarossa">Susanna Fontanarossa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeazley1911741_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeazley1911741-5">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_Columbus" title="Bartholomew Columbus">Bartolomeo</a>, Giovanni Pellegrino, and Giacomo were his brothers. Bartolomeo worked in a <a href="/wiki/Cartography" title="Cartography">cartography</a> workshop in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> for at least part of his adulthood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-8">[6]</a></sup> He also had a sister named Bianchinetta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[7]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columbus never wrote in his native language, which is presumed to have been a <a href="/wiki/Genoese_dialect" title="Genoese dialect">Genoese variety of Ligurian</a> (his name would translate in the 16th-century Genoese language as <i>Christoffa</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup> <i>Corombo</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup> <small>Ligurian pronunciation:&#160;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Ligurian" title="Help:IPA/Ligurian">[kri&#712;&#643;t&#596;ffa ku&#712;&#633;u&#331;bu]</a></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup>). In one of his writings, he says he went to sea at the age of 10. In 1470, the Columbus family moved to <a href="/wiki/Savona" title="Savona">Savona</a>, where Domenico took over a tavern. In the same year, Christopher was on a Genoese ship hired in the service of <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_of_Anjou" title="Ren&#233; of Anjou">Ren&#233; of Anjou</a> to support his attempt to conquer the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Kingdom of Naples</a>. Some modern historians have argued that he was not from Genoa but, instead, from the <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> or from <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> These competing hypotheses have generally been discounted by mainstream scholars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson19973_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson19973-16">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips199285_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips199285-17">[15]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ColombusNotesToMarcoPolo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="968" data-file-width="1334" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/ColombusNotesToMarcoPolo.jpg/240px-ColombusNotesToMarcoPolo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/ColombusNotesToMarcoPolo.jpg/360px-ColombusNotesToMarcoPolo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/ColombusNotesToMarcoPolo.jpg/480px-ColombusNotesToMarcoPolo.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ColombusNotesToMarcoPolo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Columbus\'s copy of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Travels_of_Marco_Polo" title="The Travels of Marco Polo">The Travels of Marco Polo</a></i>, with his handwritten notes in Latin written on the margins</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1473, Columbus began his apprenticeship as business agent for the important <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Centurione&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Centurione (page does not exist)">Centurione</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Di_Negro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Di Negro (page does not exist)">Di Negro</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spinola_family" title="Spinola family">Spinola</a> families of Genoa. Later, he allegedly made a trip to <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">Chios</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean</a> island then ruled by Genoa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup> In May 1476, he took part in an armed convoy sent by Genoa to carry valuable cargo to northern Europe. He docked in <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, England<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Galway" title="Galway">Galway</a>, Ireland. In 1477, he was possibly in <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeazley1911741_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeazley1911741-5">[4]</a></sup> In the autumn of 1477, he sailed on a Portuguese ship from Galway to Lisbon, where he found his brother Bartolomeo, and they continued trading for the Centurione family. Columbus based himself in Lisbon from 1477 to 1485. He married <a href="/wiki/Filipa_Moniz_Perestrelo" title="Filipa Moniz Perestrelo">Filipa Moniz Perestrelo</a>, daughter of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porto_Santo" title="Porto Santo">Porto Santo</a> governor and Portuguese nobleman of <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombard</a> origin <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Perestrello" title="Bartolomeu Perestrello">Bartolomeu Perestrello</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1479 or 1480, his son <a href="/wiki/Diego_Columbus" title="Diego Columbus">Diego Columbus</a> was born. Between 1482 and 1485, Columbus traded along the coasts of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>, reaching the Portuguese trading post of <a href="/wiki/Elmina" title="Elmina">Elmina</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guinea_coast" title="Guinea coast">Guinea coast</a> (in present-day <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB-online_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-EB-online-21">[19]</a></sup> Some records report that Filipa died sometime around 1485, while Columbus was away in Castile.  He returned to Portugal to settle her estate and take his son Diego with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> He had left Portugal for <a href="/wiki/Castile_(historical_region)" title="Castile (historical region)">Castile</a> in 1485, where he found a mistress in 1487, a 20-year-old orphan named <a href="/wiki/Beatriz_Enr%C3%ADquez_de_Arana" title="Beatriz Enr&#237;quez de Arana">Beatriz Enr&#237;quez de Arana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> It is likely that Beatriz met Columbus when he was in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="C&#243;rdoba, Spain">C&#243;rdoba</a>, a gathering site of many Genoese merchants and where the court of the Catholic Monarchs was located at intervals. Beatriz, unmarried at the time, gave birth to Columbus\'s <a href="/wiki/Legitimacy_(family_law)" title="Legitimacy (family law)">natural son</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fernando_Columbus" title="Fernando Columbus">Fernando Columbus</a> in July 1488, named for the monarch of Arag&#243;n. Columbus recognized the boy as his offspring. Columbus entrusted his older, legitimate son Diego to take care of Beatriz and pay the pension set aside for her following his death, but Diego was negligent in his duties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nAmbitious, Columbus eventually learned Latin, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, and Castilian. He read widely about astronomy, geography, and history, including the works of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Claudius_Ptolemy" title="Claudius Ptolemy">Claudius Ptolemy</a>, Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Pierre_d%27Ailly" title="Pierre d\'Ailly">Pierre d\'Ailly</a>\'s <i>Imago Mundi</i>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Travels_of_Marco_Polo" title="Travels of Marco Polo">travels of Marco Polo</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Mandeville" title="John Mandeville">John Mandeville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Natural_History_(Pliny)" title="Natural History (Pliny)">Natural History</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_II" title="Pope Pius II">Pope Pius II</a>\'s <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Historia_Rerum_Ubique_Gestarum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Historia Rerum Ubique Gestarum (page does not exist)">Historia Rerum Ubique Gestarum</a></i>. According to historian <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Morgan_(historian)" title="Edmund Morgan (historian)">Edmund Morgan</a>,<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Columbus was not a scholarly man. Yet he studied these books, made hundreds of marginal notations in them and came out with ideas about the world that were characteristically simple and strong and sometimes wrong, ...<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESMorgan_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESMorgan-25">[23]</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Throughout his life, Columbus also showed a keen interest in the Bible and in <a href="/wiki/Bible_prophecy" title="Bible prophecy">Biblical prophecies</a>, often quoting biblical texts in his letters and logs. For example, part of the argument that he submitted to the Spanish Catholic Monarchs when he sought their support for his proposed expedition to reach the Indies by sailing west was based on his reading of the <a href="/wiki/2_Esdras" title="2 Esdras">Second Book of Esdras</a> (<a href="/wiki/Esdras" title="Esdras">Ezra</a>): see <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(King_James)/II_Esdras#Chapter_6" title="wikisource:Bible (King James)/II Esdras">2 Esdras 6:42</a>, which he took to mean that the Earth is made of six parts of land to one of water. Towards the end of his life, he produced a <i><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Prophecies" title="Book of Prophecies">Book of Prophecies</a></i> in which his career as an explorer is interpreted in the light of <a href="/wiki/Christian_eschatology" title="Christian eschatology">Christian eschatology</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Apocalypticism" title="Apocalypticism">apocalypticism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-8">[6]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Quest_for_Asia">Quest for Asia</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ColombusMap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1260" data-file-width="1970" decoding="async" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/ColombusMap.jpg/350px-ColombusMap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/ColombusMap.jpg/525px-ColombusMap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/ColombusMap.jpg/700px-ColombusMap.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ColombusMap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Columbus map", drawn c.&#160;1490 in the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> workshop of Bartolomeo and Christopher Columbus<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a>\'s hegemony over Asia (the <i><a href="/wiki/Pax_Mongolica" title="Pax Mongolica">Pax Mongolica</a></i>, or <i>Mongol peace</i>), Europeans had long enjoyed <a href="/wiki/Europeans_in_Medieval_China" title="Europeans in Medieval China">a safe land passage</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indies" title="Indies">Indies</a> (then construed roughly as all of south and east Asia) and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, which were sources of valuable goods such as spices and silk. With the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">fall of Constantinople</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Turks</a> in 1453, the land route to Asia became much more difficult and dangerous. Portuguese navigators tried to find a sea way to Asia.\n</p><p>In 1470, the Florentine astronomer <a href="/wiki/Paolo_dal_Pozzo_Toscanelli" title="Paolo dal Pozzo Toscanelli">Paolo dal Pozzo Toscanelli</a> suggested to King <a href="/wiki/Afonso_V_of_Portugal" title="Afonso V of Portugal">Afonso V of Portugal</a> that sailing west would be a quicker way to reach the <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Spice Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cathay" title="Cathay">Cathay</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cipangu" title="Cipangu">Cipangu</a> than the route around Africa. Afonso rejected his proposal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> Portuguese explorers, under the leadership of King <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">John II</a>, then developed the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Route" title="Cape Route">Cape Route</a> to Asia around Africa. Major progress in this quest was achieved in 1488, when <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a> reached the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>, in what is now South Africa. Meanwhile, in the 1480s, the Columbus brothers had picked up Toscanelli\'s suggestion and proposed a plan to reach the Indies by sailing west across the "Ocean Sea", i.e., the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a>. However, Dias\'s discovery had shifted the interests of Portuguese seafaring to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeast_passage" title="Southeast passage">southeast passage</a>, which complicated Columbus\'s proposals significantly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-28">[26]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_considerations">Geographical considerations</span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Washington_Irving" title="Washington Irving">Washington Irving</a>\'s 1828 biography of Columbus popularized the idea that Columbus had difficulty obtaining support for his plan because many Catholic theologians insisted that the <a href="/wiki/Flat_Earth" title="Flat Earth">Earth was flat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-book3_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-book3-29">[27]</a></sup> In fact, nearly all educated Westerners had understood, at least since the time of <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a>, that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myth_of_the_Flat_Earth" title="Myth of the Flat Earth">the Earth is spherical</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-28">[26]</a></sup> The sphericity of the Earth is also accounted for in the work of <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a>, on which <a href="/wiki/Geocentric_model" title="Geocentric model">medieval astronomy</a> was largely based. Christian writers whose works clearly reflect the conviction that the Earth is spherical include Saint <a href="/wiki/Bede" title="Bede">Bede</a> the Venerable in his <i>Reckoning of Time</i>, written around AD 723. In Columbus\'s time, the techniques of <a href="/wiki/Celestial_navigation" title="Celestial navigation">celestial navigation</a>, which use the position of the sun and the stars in the sky, together with the understanding that the Earth is a sphere, had long been in use by astronomers and were beginning to be implemented by mariners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As far back as the 3rd century BC, <a href="/wiki/Eratosthenes" title="Eratosthenes">Eratosthenes</a> had correctly computed the circumference of the Earth by using simple geometry and studying the shadows cast by objects at two remote locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> In the 1st century BC, <a href="/wiki/Posidonius" title="Posidonius">Posidonius</a> confirmed Eratosthenes\'s results by comparing stellar observations at two separate locations. These measurements were widely known among scholars, but confusion about the old-fashioned units of distance in which they were expressed led to some debate about the size of the Earth.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atlantic_Ocean,_Toscanelli,_1474.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1215" data-file-width="1990" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Atlantic_Ocean%2C_Toscanelli%2C_1474.jpg/300px-Atlantic_Ocean%2C_Toscanelli%2C_1474.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Atlantic_Ocean%2C_Toscanelli%2C_1474.jpg/450px-Atlantic_Ocean%2C_Toscanelli%2C_1474.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Atlantic_Ocean%2C_Toscanelli%2C_1474.jpg/600px-Atlantic_Ocean%2C_Toscanelli%2C_1474.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atlantic_Ocean,_Toscanelli,_1474.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Paolo_dal_Pozzo_Toscanelli" title="Paolo dal Pozzo Toscanelli">Toscanelli</a>\'s notions of the geography of the Atlantic Ocean (shown superimposed on a modern map), which directly influenced Columbus\'s plans.</div></div></div>\n<p>From d\'Ailly\'s <i>Imago Mundi</i> Columbus learned of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahmad_ibn_Muhammad_ibn_Kath%C4%ABr_al-Fargh%C4%81n%C4%AB" title="Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Kath&#299;r al-Fargh&#257;n&#299;">Alfraganus</a>\'s estimate that a degree of <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> (or a degree of <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a> along the equator) spanned 56<span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;"><span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">2</span><span class="visualhide">/</span><span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">3</span></span> miles, but did not realize that this was expressed in the <a href="/wiki/Arabic_mile" title="Arabic mile">Arabic mile</a> rather than the shorter <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_mile" title="Roman mile">Roman mile</a> with which he was familiar (1,480&#160;m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> He therefore estimated the circumference of the Earth to be about 30,200&#160;km, whereas the correct value is 40,000&#160;km (25,000&#160;mi).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Furthermore, most scholars accepted <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a>\'s estimate that <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> spanned 180&#176; <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a>, rather than the actual 130&#176; (to the Chinese mainland) or 150&#176; (to Japan at the latitude of Spain). Columbus, for his part, believed the even higher estimate of <a href="/wiki/Marinus_of_Tyre" title="Marinus of Tyre">Marinus of Tyre</a>, which put the longitudinal span of the Eurasian landmass at 225&#176;, leaving only 135&#176; of water. He also believed that Japan (which he called "Cipangu", following <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a>) was much larger, farther to the east from China ("Cathay"), and closer to the equator than it is, and that there were inhabited islands even farther to the east than Japan, including the mythical <a href="/wiki/Antillia" title="Antillia">Antillia</a>, which he thought might lie not much farther to the west than the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>. In this, he was influenced by the ideas of Florentine astronomer, <a href="/wiki/Paolo_dal_Pozzo_Toscanelli" title="Paolo dal Pozzo Toscanelli">Paolo dal Pozzo Toscanelli</a>, who corresponded with Columbus in 1474<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> and who also defended the feasibility of a westward route to Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morison-Admiral_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morison-Admiral-36">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columbus therefore estimated the distance from the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> to Japan to be about 3,000 Italian miles (3,700&#160;km, or 2,300 statute miles). The true figure is now known to be vastly larger: about 20,000&#160;km.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips1992110_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips1992110-37">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[c]</a></sup> No ship in the 15th century could have carried enough food and fresh water for such a long voyage, and the dangers involved in navigating through the uncharted ocean would have been formidable. Most European navigators reasonably concluded that a westward voyage from Europe to Asia was unfeasible. The Catholic Monarchs, however, having completed <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">an expensive war</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, were eager to obtain a competitive edge over other European countries in the quest for trade with the Indies. Columbus\'s project, though far-fetched, held the promise of such an advantage.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nautical_considerations">Nautical considerations</span></h3>\n<p>Though Columbus was wrong about the number of degrees of longitude that separated Europe from the Far East and about the distance that each degree represented, he did possess valuable knowledge about the <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a>, which would prove to be the key to his successful navigation of the Atlantic Ocean. During his first voyage in 1492, the brisk trade winds from the east, commonly called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Easterlies" title="Easterlies">easterlies</a>", propelled Columbus\'s fleet for five weeks, from the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> to <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>. The precise first land sighting and landing point was <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador_Island" title="San Salvador Island">San Salvador Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-28">[26]</a></sup> To return to Spain against this prevailing wind would have required several months of an arduous sailing technique, called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Close_hauled#Close_hauled" title="Close hauled">beating</a>, during which food and drinkable water would probably have been exhausted.\n</p><p>Instead, Columbus returned home by following the curving trade winds northeastward to the middle latitudes of the North Atlantic, where he was able to catch the "<a href="/wiki/Westerlies" title="Westerlies">westerlies</a>" that blow eastward to the coast of Western Europe. There, in turn, the winds curve southward towards the Iberian Peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup>\n</p><p>It is unclear whether Columbus learned about the winds from his own sailing experience or if he had heard about them from others. The corresponding technique for efficient travel in the Atlantic appears to have been exploited first by the Portuguese, who referred to it as the <i><a href="/wiki/Volta_do_mar" title="Volta do mar">Volta do mar</a></i> ("turn of the sea"). Columbus\'s knowledge of the Atlantic wind patterns was, however, imperfect at the time of his first voyage. By sailing directly due west from the Canary Islands during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Atlantic_hurricane_seasons" title="List of Atlantic hurricane seasons">hurricane season</a>, skirting the so-called <a href="/wiki/Horse_latitudes" title="Horse latitudes">horse latitudes</a> of the mid-Atlantic, Columbus risked either being becalmed or running into a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a>, both of which, by chance, he avoided.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morison-Admiral_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morison-Admiral-36">[34]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quest_for_financial_support_for_a_voyage">Quest for financial support for a voyage</span></h3>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Columbus&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_offers_his_services_to_the_King_of_Portugal_-_Daniel_Nicholas_Chodowiecki_(cropped).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="415" decoding="async" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Columbus_offers_his_services_to_the_King_of_Portugal_-_Daniel_Nicholas_Chodowiecki_%28cropped%29.png/170px-Columbus_offers_his_services_to_the_King_of_Portugal_-_Daniel_Nicholas_Chodowiecki_%28cropped%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Columbus_offers_his_services_to_the_King_of_Portugal_-_Daniel_Nicholas_Chodowiecki_%28cropped%29.png/255px-Columbus_offers_his_services_to_the_King_of_Portugal_-_Daniel_Nicholas_Chodowiecki_%28cropped%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Columbus_offers_his_services_to_the_King_of_Portugal_-_Daniel_Nicholas_Chodowiecki_%28cropped%29.png/340px-Columbus_offers_his_services_to_the_King_of_Portugal_-_Daniel_Nicholas_Chodowiecki_%28cropped%29.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_offers_his_services_to_the_King_of_Portugal_-_Daniel_Nicholas_Chodowiecki_(cropped).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Columbus offers his services to the King of Portugal</i>; <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Chodowiecki" title="Daniel Chodowiecki">Chodowiecki</a>, 17th c.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1485, Columbus presented his plans to King <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">John II of Portugal</a>. He proposed that the king equip three sturdy ships and grant Columbus one year\'s time to sail out into the Atlantic, search for a western route to the <a href="/wiki/Orient" title="Orient">Orient</a>, and return. Columbus also requested he be made "Great Admiral of the Ocean", appointed governor of any and all lands he discovered, and given one-tenth of all revenue from those lands. The king submitted Columbus\'s proposal to his experts, who rejected it. It was their considered opinion that Columbus\'s estimation of a travel distance of 2,400 miles (3,860&#160;km) was, in fact, far too low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morison-Admiral_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-Morison-Admiral-36">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1488, Columbus again appealed to the court of Portugal, resulting in John II again inviting him for an audience. That meeting also proved unsuccessful, in part because not long afterwards <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a> returned to Portugal with news of his successful rounding of the southern tip of Africa (near the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>). With an eastern sea route to Asia apparently at hand, King John was no longer interested in Columbus\'s far-fetched project.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1147" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG/220px-Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG/330px-Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG/440px-Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Columbus before the Queen</i>, as imagined<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze" title="Emanuel Gottlieb Leutze">Emanuel Gottlieb Leutze</a>, 1843</div></div></div>\n<p>Columbus traveled from Portugal to both <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venice</a>, but he received encouragement from neither. He had also dispatched his brother <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_Columbus" title="Bartholomew Columbus">Bartholomew</a> to the court of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a> to inquire whether the English crown might sponsor his expedition, but also without success.\n</p><p>Columbus had sought an audience from the monarchs <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">Ferdinand II of Aragon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Isabella I of Castile</a>, who had united several kingdoms in the Iberian Peninsula by marrying and were ruling together. On 1 May 1486, permission having been granted, Columbus presented his plans to Queen Isabella, who, in turn, referred it to a committee. After the passing of much time, the <a href="/wiki/Expert" title="Expert">savants</a> of Spain, like their counterparts in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portugal</a>, replied that Columbus had grossly underestimated the distance to Asia. They pronounced the idea impractical and advised their Royal Highnesses to pass on the proposed venture.\n</p><p>However, to keep Columbus from taking his ideas elsewhere, and perhaps to keep their options open, the Catholic Monarchs gave him an annual allowance of 12,000 <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maravedis" title="Maravedis">maravedis</a></i> and, in 1489, furnished him with a letter ordering all cities and towns under their domain to provide him food and lodging at no cost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agreement_with_the_Spanish_crown">Agreement with the Spanish crown</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_Fleet_1893_Issue.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="1521" decoding="async" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Columbus_Fleet_1893_Issue.jpg/330px-Columbus_Fleet_1893_Issue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Columbus_Fleet_1893_Issue.jpg/495px-Columbus_Fleet_1893_Issue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Columbus_Fleet_1893_Issue.jpg/660px-Columbus_Fleet_1893_Issue.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_Fleet_1893_Issue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Flagship of Columbus and the Fleet of Columbus. 400th Anniversary Issues of 1893. (<a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus#Voyages_and_events" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">On ships.</a>)</div></div></div>\n<p>After continually lobbying at the <a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">Spanish court</a> and two years of negotiations, he finally had success in January 1492. Ferdinand and Isabella had just conquered <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Granada" title="Emirate of Granada">last Muslim stronghold</a> on the Iberian Peninsula, and they received Columbus in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="C&#243;rdoba, Spain">C&#243;rdoba</a>, in the <i><a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_de_los_Reyes_Cristianos" title="Alc&#225;zar de los Reyes Cristianos">Alc&#225;zar</a></i> castle. Isabella turned him down on the advice of her <a href="/wiki/Confessor" title="Confessor">confessor</a>. Columbus was leaving town by mule in despair when Ferdinand intervened. Isabella then sent a royal guard to fetch him, and Ferdinand later claimed credit for being "the principal cause why those islands were discovered".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips1992132_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips1992132-43">[40]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the April 1492 "<a href="/wiki/Capitulations_of_Santa_Fe" title="Capitulations of Santa Fe">Capitulations of Santa Fe</a>", King Ferdinand and Queen Isabella promised Columbus that if he succeeded he would be given the rank of Admiral of the Ocean Sea and appointed Viceroy and Governor of all the new lands he could claim for Spain. He had the right to nominate three persons, from whom the sovereigns would choose one, for any office in the new lands. He would be entitled to 10 percent of all the revenues from the new lands in perpetuity. Additionally, he would also have the option of buying one-eighth interest in any commercial venture with the new lands and receive one-eighth of the profits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morison-Admiral_36-3"><a href="#cite_note-Morison-Admiral-36">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columbus was later arrested in 1500 and dismissed from his posts. He and his sons, Diego and Fernando, then conducted a lengthy series of court cases against the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castilian crown</a>, known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Pleitos_colombinos" title="Pleitos colombinos">pleitos colombinos</a></i>, alleging that the Crown had illegally reneged on its contractual obligations to Columbus and his heirs. The Columbus family had some success in their first litigation, as a judgment of 1511 confirmed Diego\'s position as Viceroy, but reduced his powers. Diego resumed litigation in 1512, which lasted until 1536, and further disputes continued until 1790.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Voyages">Voyages</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">Voyages of Christopher Columbus</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Viajes_de_colon_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="343" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Viajes_de_colon_en.svg/350px-Viajes_de_colon_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Viajes_de_colon_en.svg/525px-Viajes_de_colon_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Viajes_de_colon_en.svg/700px-Viajes_de_colon_en.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Viajes_de_colon_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The voyages of Christopher Columbus</div></div></div>\n<p>Between 1492 and 1503, Columbus completed four round-trip voyages between Spain and the Americas, each voyage being sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>. On his first voyage, he independently discovered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">the Americas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_declination" title="Magnetic declination">magnetic declination</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[d]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[43]</a></sup> These voyages marked the beginning of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" title="European ethnic groups">European</a> <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">exploration</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_colonialism" title="History of colonialism">colonization</a> of <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">the American continents</a>, and are thus of enormous significance in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Western_civilization" title="History of Western civilization">Western history</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-8">[6]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columbus always insisted, in the face of mounting evidence to the contrary, that the lands that he visited during those voyages were part of the <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a> continent, as previously described by <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> and other European travelers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-8">[6]</a></sup> Columbus\'s refusal to accept that the lands he had visited and claimed for Spain were not part of Asia might explain, in part, why the American continent was named after the <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florentine</a> explorer <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a> and not after Columbus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[44]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_voyage">First voyage</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_first_voyage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="597" data-file-width="1001" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Columbus_first_voyage.jpg/350px-Columbus_first_voyage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Columbus_first_voyage.jpg/525px-Columbus_first_voyage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Columbus_first_voyage.jpg/700px-Columbus_first_voyage.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_first_voyage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>First voyage. Modern place names in black, Columbus\'s place names in blue</div></div></div>\n<p>On the evening of 3 August 1492, Columbus departed from <a href="/wiki/Palos_de_la_Frontera" title="Palos de la Frontera">Palos de la Frontera</a> with three ships. The largest was a <a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">carrack</a> (Spanish: <i>nao</i>), the <i><a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_(ship)" title="Santa Mar&#237;a (ship)">Santa Mar&#237;a</a></i> ex-<i>Gallega</i> ("Galician")<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag needs further explanation. (June 2018)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. The other two were smaller <a href="/wiki/Caravel" title="Caravel">caravels</a>. The name of one is lost: it is known today only by the <a href="/wiki/Nickname" title="Nickname">nickname</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Pinta_(ship)" title="Pinta (ship)">Pinta</a></i>, which in Castilian of the time meant "painted one".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[45]</a></sup> The <i>Santa Clara</i> was nicknamed affectionately the <i><a href="/wiki/Ni%C3%B1a" title="Ni&#241;a">Ni&#241;a</a></i> ("the little one"), a pun on the name of her owner, Juan Ni&#241;o of Moguer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[46]</a></sup> The monarchs forced the citizens of Palos to contribute to the expedition. The <i>Santa Mar&#237;a</i> was owned by <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_la_Cosa" title="Juan de la Cosa">Juan de la Cosa</a> and captained by Columbus. The <i>Pinta</i> and the <i>Ni&#241;a</i> were piloted by the <a href="/wiki/Pinz%C3%B3n_brothers" title="Pinz&#243;n brothers">Pinz&#243;n brothers</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Alonso_Pinz%C3%B3n" title="Mart&#237;n Alonso Pinz&#243;n">Mart&#237;n Alonso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Y%C3%A1%C3%B1ez_Pinz%C3%B3n" title="Vicente Y&#225;&#241;ez Pinz&#243;n">Vicente Y&#225;&#241;ez</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_28-3"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-28">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columbus first sailed to the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, which belonged to <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castile</a>. He restocked provisions and made repairs in <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, then departed from <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_de_La_Gomera" title="San Sebasti&#225;n de La Gomera">San Sebasti&#225;n de La Gomera</a> on 6 September, for what turned out to be a five-week voyage across the ocean. At about 2:00 in the morning of 12 October (21 October, Gregorian Calendar New Style), a lookout on the <i>Pinta</i>, <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_de_Triana" title="Rodrigo de Triana">Rodrigo de Triana</a> (also known as Juan Rodr&#237;guez Bermeo), spotted land, and immediately alerted the rest of the crew with a shout. Thereupon, the captain of the <i>Pinta</i>, Mart&#237;n Alonso Pinz&#243;n, verified the discovery and alerted Columbus by firing a <a href="/wiki/Lombard_(gun)" title="Lombard (gun)">lombard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[47]</a></sup> Columbus later maintained that he himself had already seen a light on the land a few hours earlier, thereby claiming for himself the lifetime pension promised by Ferdinand and Isabella to the first person to sight land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_28-4"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-28">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columbus called the island (in what is now <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>) <i>San Salvador</i> (meaning "Holy Savior"); the natives called it <a href="/wiki/Guanahani" title="Guanahani">Guanahani</a>. Exactly which island in the Bahamas this corresponds to is unresolved. Based on primary accounts and on what one would expect from the geographic positions of the islands given Columbus\'s course, the prime candidates are <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador_Island" title="San Salvador Island">San Salvador Island</a> (so named in 1925 on the theory that it was Columbus\'s San Salvador),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Samana_Cay" title="Samana Cay">Samana Cay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Plana_Cays" title="Plana Cays">Plana Cays</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_28-5"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-28">[26]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Landing_of_Columbus_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1971" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/220px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/330px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/440px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Landing_of_Columbus_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Landing of Columbus</i> (12 October 1492), painting by <a href="/wiki/John_Vanderlyn" title="John Vanderlyn">John Vanderlyn</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_Peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous Peoples of the Americas">indigenous people</a> he encountered, the <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_people" title="Lucayan people">Lucayan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" title="Ta&#237;no people">Ta&#237;no</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" title="Arawak peoples">Arawak</a>, were peaceful and friendly. He called the inhabitants of the lands that he visited <i>indios</i> (Spanish for "Indians").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoxie_1996_p._54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hoxie_1996_p.-54">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herbst1997_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herbst1997-55">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilton2004_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wilton2004-56">[52]</a></sup> Noting their gold ear ornaments, Columbus took some of the Arawaks prisoner and insisted that they guide him to the source of the gold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zinn_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zinn-57">[53]</a></sup> From the entry in <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus%27s_journal" title="Christopher Columbus\'s journal">his journal</a> of 12 October 1492, in which he wrote of them: "Many of the men I have seen have scars on their bodies, and when I made signs to them to find out how this happened, they indicated that people from other nearby islands come to San Salvador to capture them; they defend themselves the best they can. I believe that people from the mainland come here to take them as slaves. They ought to make good and skilled servants, for they repeat very quickly whatever we say to them. I think they can very easily be made Christians, for they seem to have no religion. If it pleases our Lord, I will take six of them to Your Highnesses when I depart, in order that they may learn our language."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[54]</a></sup> Columbus noted that their primitive weapons and military tactics made them susceptible to easy conquest, writing, "these people are very simple in war-like matters &#8230; I could conquer the whole of them with 50 men, and govern them as I pleased."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[55]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columbus also explored the northeast coast of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, where he landed on 28 October. On 22 November, Mart&#237;n Alonso Pinz&#243;n took the <i>Pinta</i> on an unauthorized expedition in search of an island called "Babeque" or "Baneque", which the natives had told him was rich in gold. Columbus, for his part, continued to the northern coast of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, where he landed on 5 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pickering-1st_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pickering-1st-60">[56]</a></sup> There, the <i>Santa Mar&#237;a</i> ran aground on Christmas Day 1492 and had to be abandoned. The wreck was used as a target for cannon fire to impress the native peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_28-6"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-28">[26]</a></sup> Columbus was received by the native <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guacanagari" title="Guacanagari">Guacanagari</a>, who gave him permission to leave some of his men behind. Columbus left 39 men, including <a href="/wiki/Luis_de_Torres" title="Luis de Torres">Luis de Torres</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">converso</a></i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interpreter" title="Interpreter">interpreter</a>, who spoke <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and founded the settlement of <i><a href="/wiki/La_Navidad" title="La Navidad">La Navidad</a></i> at the site of present-day Bord de Mer de Limonade, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[57]</a></sup> Columbus took more natives prisoner and continued his exploration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zinn_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zinn-57">[53]</a></sup> He kept sailing along the northern coast of Hispaniola with a single ship, until he encountered Pinz&#243;n and the <i>Pinta</i> on 6 January.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WC_Delacroix,Eugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="888" data-file-width="1168" decoding="async" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg/250px-WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg/375px-WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg/500px-WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WC_Delacroix,Eugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The return of Christopher Columbus; his audience before King Ferdinand and Queen Isabella</i>, painting by <a href="/wiki/Eug%C3%A8ne_Delacroix" title="Eug&#232;ne Delacroix">Eug&#232;ne Delacroix</a></div></div></div>\n<table class="mbox-small noprint" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:His_Master%27s_Voice_(small).png"><img alt="His Master\'s Voice (small).png" data-file-height="180" data-file-width="240" decoding="async" height="53" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/His_Master%27s_Voice_%28small%29.png/140px-His_Master%27s_Voice_%28small%29.png 2x" width="70"/></a></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist"
