style="line-height:1.1em"><hr/><span class="selfreference"><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>On 13 January 1493, Columbus made his last stop of this voyage in the New World, in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Rinc%C3%B3n" title="Bay of Rinc&#243;n">Bay of Rinc&#243;n</a> at the eastern end of the <a href="/wiki/Saman%C3%A1_Peninsula" title="Saman&#225; Peninsula">Saman&#225; Peninsula</a> in northeast Hispaniola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[58]</a></sup> There he encountered the warlike <a href="/wiki/Ciguayos" title="Ciguayos">Cig&#252;ayos</a>, the only natives who offered violent resistance during his first voyage to the Americas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[59]</a></sup> The Cig&#252;ayos refused to trade the amount of bows and arrows that Columbus desired; in the ensuing clash one Ciguayo was stabbed in the buttocks and another wounded with an arrow in his chest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[60]</a></sup> Because of this and because of the Cig&#252;ayos\' use of arrows, he called the inlet where he met them <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Arrows" title="Bay of Arrows">the Bay of Arrows (or Gulf of Arrows)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[61]</a></sup> Columbus kidnapped about 10 to 25 natives and took them back with him (only seven or eight of the natives arrived in Spain alive).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELoewen1995_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoewen1995-66">[62]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columbus headed for Spain on the <i>Ni&#241;a</i>, but a storm separated him from the <i>Pinta,</i> and forced the <i>Ni&#241;a</i> to stop at the island of Santa Maria in the Azores. Half of his crew went ashore to say prayers in a chapel to give thanks for having survived the storm. But while praying, they were imprisoned by the governor of the island, ostensibly on suspicion of being pirates.  After a two-day standoff, the prisoners were released, and Columbus again set sail for Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another storm forced him into the port at <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_28-7"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-28">[26]</a></sup> He anchored next to the King\'s harbor patrol ship on 4 March 1493 in Portugal. There, he was interviewed by <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a>, who had rounded the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> a few years earlier, in 1488&#8211;1489. Dias\'s success had complicated Columbus\'s attempts to secure funding from the Portuguese court because the sure route to the Indies that Dias pioneered made a risky, conjectural western route unnecessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_28-8"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-28">[26]</a></sup> Not finding King <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">John II of Portugal</a> in Lisbon, Columbus wrote a letter to him and waited for John\'s reply. John asked Columbus to go to <i>Vale do Para&#237;so</i> north of Lisbon to meet him. Relations between Portugal and Castile were poor at the time. Columbus went to meet with John at <i>Vale do Para&#237;so</i>. Hearing of Columbus\'s discoveries, John told him that he believed the voyage to be in violation of the 1479 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Alc%C3%A1%C3%A7ovas" title="Treaty of Alc&#225;&#231;ovas">Treaty of Alc&#225;&#231;ovas</a>.\n</p><p>After spending more than a week in Portugal, and paying his respects to <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Viseu" title="Eleanor of Viseu">Eleanor of Viseu</a>, Columbus again set sail for Spain. <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> was a young boy and a ward of Eleanor\'s court; it is likely he saw Columbus during this visit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murphy_28-9"><a href="#cite_note-murphy-28">[26]</a></sup> After departing, and after reportedly being saved from assassins by King John, Columbus crossed the bar of Saltes and entered the harbor of Palos de la Frontera on 15 March 1493. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus_Letter_on_the_First_Voyage" title="Columbus Letter on the First Voyage">Word of his finding new lands</a> rapidly spread throughout Europe.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_voyage">Second voyage</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_second_voyage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="563" data-file-width="1001" decoding="async" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Columbus_second_voyage.jpg/350px-Columbus_second_voyage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Columbus_second_voyage.jpg/525px-Columbus_second_voyage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Columbus_second_voyage.jpg/700px-Columbus_second_voyage.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_second_voyage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Columbus\'s second voyage</div></div></div>\n<p>Columbus left the port of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="C&#225;diz">C&#225;diz</a> on 24 September 1493, with a fleet of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus%27s_second_voyage" title="Columbus\'s second voyage">17 ships</a> carrying 1,200 men and the supplies to establish permanent colonies in the New World. The passengers included priests, farmers, and soldiers, who would be the new colonists. This reflected the new policy of creating not just "colonies of exploitation", but also "colonies of settlement" from which to launch missions dedicated to converting the natives to Christianity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[64]</a></sup> Modern studies suggest that, as reported by the <i>Washington Post</i>, "crew members may have included free black Africans who arrived in the New World about a decade before the slave trade began."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As in the first voyage, the fleet stopped at the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, from which it departed on 13 October, following a more southerly course than on the previous expedition. On 3 November, Columbus sighted a rugged island that he named <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> (Latin for Sunday); later that day, he landed at <a href="/wiki/Marie-Galante" title="Marie-Galante">Marie-Galante</a>, which he named <i>Santa Mar&#237;a la Galante</i>. After sailing past <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Les_Saintes" title="Les Saintes">Les Saintes</a> (<i>Los Santos</i>, "The Saints"), he arrived at the island of <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, which he named <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Guadalupe" title="Santa Mar&#237;a de Guadalupe">Santa Mar&#237;a de Guadalupe</a> de Extremadura</i>, after the image of the Virgin Mary venerated at the Spanish monastery of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Villuercas" title="Villuercas">Villuercas</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Guadalupe,_C%C3%A1ceres" title="Guadalupe, C&#225;ceres">Guadalupe, C&#225;ceres</a>, Spain. He explored that island from 4 to 10 November.\n</p><p>Michele da Cuneo, Columbus\'s childhood friend from <a href="/wiki/Savona" title="Savona">Savona</a>, sailed with Columbus during the second voyage and wrote: "In my opinion, since Genoa was Genoa, there was never born a man so well equipped and expert in the art of navigation as the said lord Admiral."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup> Columbus named the small island of "Saona&#160;... to honor Michele da Cuneo, his friend from Savona."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[67]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The same childhood friend reported in a letter that Columbus had provided one of the captured indigenous women to him. He wrote, "While I was in the boat, I captured a very beautiful Carib woman, whom the said Lord Admiral gave to me. When I had taken her to my cabin she was naked&#8212;as was their custom. I was filled with a desire to take my pleasure with her and attempted to satisfy my desire. She was unwilling, and so treated me with her nails that I wished I had never begun. But&#8212;to cut a long story short&#8212;I then took a piece of rope and whipped her soundly, and she let forth such incredible screams that you would not have believed your ears. Eventually we came to such terms, I assure you, that you would have thought that she had been brought up in a school for whores."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[68]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Inspiracion_de_Cristobal_Colon_by_Jose_Maria_Obregon,_1856.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3011" data-file-width="2074" decoding="async" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Inspiracion_de_Cristobal_Colon_by_Jose_Maria_Obregon%2C_1856.jpg/170px-Inspiracion_de_Cristobal_Colon_by_Jose_Maria_Obregon%2C_1856.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Inspiracion_de_Cristobal_Colon_by_Jose_Maria_Obregon%2C_1856.jpg/255px-Inspiracion_de_Cristobal_Colon_by_Jose_Maria_Obregon%2C_1856.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Inspiracion_de_Cristobal_Colon_by_Jose_Maria_Obregon%2C_1856.jpg/340px-Inspiracion_de_Cristobal_Colon_by_Jose_Maria_Obregon%2C_1856.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Inspiracion_de_Cristobal_Colon_by_Jose_Maria_Obregon,_1856.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Inspiration of Christopher Columbus</i> by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Velasco_G%C3%B3mez" title="Jos&#233; Mar&#237;a Velasco G&#243;mez">Jos&#233; Mar&#237;a Obreg&#243;n</a>, 1856</div></div></div>\n<p>Pedro de las Casas, father of the priest <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_de_las_Casas" title="Bartolom&#233; de las Casas">Bartolom&#233; de las Casas</a>, also accompanied Columbus on this voyage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-traboulay_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-traboulay-73">[69]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The exact course of Columbus\'s voyage through the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> is debated, but it seems likely that he turned north, sighting and naming several islands, including:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a> (for Santa Mar&#237;a de Montserrate, after the Blessed Virgin of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monastery_of_Montserrat" title="Monastery of Montserrat">Monastery of Montserrat</a>, which is located on the Mountain of Montserrat, in Catalonia, Spain),</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a> (after a church in <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, Spain, called Santa Mar&#237;a la Antigua, meaning "Old St. Mary\'s"),</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Redonda" title="Redonda">Redonda</a> (<i>Santa Mar&#237;a la Redonda</i>, Spanish for "St. Mary the Round", owing to the island\'s shape),</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> (derived from the Spanish <i>Nuestra Se&#241;ora de las Nieves</i>, "Our Lady of the Snows", because Columbus thought the clouds over Nevis Peak made the island resemble a snow-capped mountain),</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a> (for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Christopher" title="St. Christopher">St. Christopher</a>, patron of sailors and travelers),</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> (for the early Roman martyr, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Eustace" title="Saint Eustace">St. Eustachius</a>),</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> (after the Biblical <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Sheba" title="Queen of Sheba">Queen of Sheba</a>),</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a> (<i>San Mart&#237;n</i>), and</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a> (from the Spanish <i>Santa Cruz</i>, meaning "<a href="/wiki/Christian_cross" title="Christian cross">Holy Cross</a>").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[70]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Columbus also sighted the chain of the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a>, which he named <i>Islas de Santa &#218;rsula y las Once Mil V&#237;rgenes</i>, "Islands of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Ursula" title="Saint Ursula">Saint Ursula</a> and the 11,000 Virgins" (shortened, both on maps of the time and in common parlance, to <i>Islas V&#237;rgenes</i>). He also named the islands of <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Gorda" title="Virgin Gorda">Virgin Gorda</a> ("Fat Virgin"), <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">Tortola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Island" title="Peter Island">Peter Island</a> (<i>San Pedro</i>).\n</p><p>One of the first skirmishes between <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native Americans</a> and Europeans since the time of the Vikings occurred on 14 November, when at <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a>, Columbus\'s men rescued two native boys from several <a href="/wiki/Human_cannibalism" title="Human cannibalism">cannibalistic</a> <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips1992[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid8jhtmzLlX70CpgPA197_197&#8211;98]_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips1992[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid8jhtmzLlX70CpgPA197_197&#8211;98]-75">[71]</a></sup> Columbus\'s men pursued the Carib canoe, which met them with arrows. Several Europeans were wounded, but they killed all of the Caribs, and learned that the two boys had recently been castrated by their captors. Columbus continued to the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a>, and landed in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, which he named <i>San Juan Bautista</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips1992198_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhillips,_JrPhillips1992198-76">[72]</a></sup> in honor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_John_the_Baptist" title="Saint John the Baptist">Saint John the Baptist</a> (a name that was later given to the capital city of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>).\n</p><p>On 22 November, Columbus returned to Hispaniola, where he intended to visit the fort of <a href="/wiki/La_Navidad" title="La Navidad">La Navidad</a>, built during his first voyage and located on the northern coast of <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>. Columbus found the fort in ruins, destroyed by the native <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" title="Ta&#237;no people">Taino</a> people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[73]</a></sup> Among the ruins were the corpses of 11 of the 39 Spaniards who had stayed behind as the first colonists in the New World.\n</p><p>Columbus then sailed more than 100 kilometres (62 miles) eastwards along the northern coast of Hispaniola, establishing a new settlement, which he called <a href="/wiki/La_Isabela" title="La Isabela">La Isabela</a>, in the present-day <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[74]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/La_Isabela" title="La Isabela">La Isabela</a> proved to be poorly located and the settlement was short-lived.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_voyage">Third voyage</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_third_voyage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="638" data-file-width="901" decoding="async" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Columbus_third_voyage.jpg/350px-Columbus_third_voyage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Columbus_third_voyage.jpg/525px-Columbus_third_voyage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Columbus_third_voyage.jpg/700px-Columbus_third_voyage.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_third_voyage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Third voyage</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the abstract of Columbus\'s journal made by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_de_Las_Casas" title="Bartolom&#233; de Las Casas">Bartolom&#233; de Las Casas</a>, the objective of the third voyage was to verify the existence of a continent that King John II of Portugal suggested was located to the southwest of the Cape Verde Islands. King John reportedly knew of the existence of such a mainland because "canoes had been found which set out from the coast of Guinea [West Africa] and sailed to the west with merchandise."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 30 May 1498, Columbus left with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus%27s_third_voyage" title="Columbus\'s third voyage">six ships</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sanl%C3%BAcar_de_Barrameda" title="Sanl&#250;car de Barrameda">Sanl&#250;car, Spain</a>, for his third trip to the New World. Three of the ships headed directly for Hispaniola with much-needed supplies, while Columbus took the other three in an exploration of what might lie to the south of the Caribbean islands he had already visited, including a hoped-for passage to continental Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minster-3rd_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Minster-3rd-81">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columbus led his fleet to the Portuguese island of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porto_Santo" title="Porto Santo">Porto Santo</a>, his wife\'s native land. He then sailed to <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and spent some time there with the Portuguese captain Jo&#227;o Gon&#231;alves da Camara, before sailing to the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>. As he crossed the Atlantic, Columbus discovered that the angle between North as indicated by a magnetic compass and North as measured by the position of the <a href="/wiki/Pole_star" title="Pole star">pole star</a> changed with his position (a phenomenon now known as "<a href="/wiki/Magnetic_declination" title="Magnetic declination">compass variation</a>"). He would later use his previous measurements of the compass variation to adjust his reckoning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB-online_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-EB-online-21">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After being becalmed for several days in the <a href="/wiki/Doldrums" title="Doldrums">doldrums</a> of the mid-Atlantic, Columbus\'s fleet regained its wind and, dangerously low on water, turned north in the direction of <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, which Columbus had visited in his previous voyage. The ships arrived at King John\'s hypothesized continent, which is <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, when they sighted the land of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> on 31 July approaching from the southeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[78]</a></sup> The fleet sailed along the southern coast and entered <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Channel" title="Columbus Channel">Dragon\'s Mouth</a>, anchoring near <a href="/wiki/Soldado_Rock" title="Soldado Rock">Soldado Rock</a> where they made contact with a group of native <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Amerindians</a> in canoes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[79]</a></sup> Columbus then landed on Trinidad at <a href="/wiki/Icacos_Point" title="Icacos Point">Icacos Point</a> (which he named <i>Punta de Arenal</i>) on 2 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[80]</a></sup> After resupplying with food and water, from 4 to 12 August Columbus explored the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Paria" title="Gulf of Paria">Gulf of Paria</a>, which separates Trinidad from what is now <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, near the delta of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orinoco_River" title="Orinoco River">Orinoco River</a>. He then touched the mainland of South America at the <a href="/wiki/Paria_Peninsula" title="Paria Peninsula">Paria Peninsula</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>Exploring the new continent, Columbus correctly interpreted the enormous quantity of fresh water that the Orinoco delivered into the Atlantic Ocean as evidence that he had reached a large landmass rather than another island. He also speculated that the new continent might be the location of the biblical <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Eden" title="Garden of Eden">Garden of Eden</a>. He then sailed to the islands of <a href="/wiki/Chacachacare" title="Chacachacare">Chacachacare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margarita_Island" title="Margarita Island">Margarita</a>. He sighted <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a> (which he named "Bella Forma") and <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> (which he named "Concepci&#243;n".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[81]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In poor health, Columbus returned to <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> on 19 August, only to find that many of the Spanish settlers of the new colony were in rebellion against his rule, claiming that Columbus had misled them about the supposedly bountiful riches of the New World. A number of returning settlers and sailors lobbied against Columbus at the <a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">Spanish court</a>, accusing him and his brothers of gross mismanagement. Columbus had some of his crew hanged for disobedience. He had an economic interest in the enslavement of the Hispaniola natives and for that reason was not eager to baptize them, which attracted criticism from some churchmen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-varela_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-varela-86">[82]</a></sup> An entry in his journal from September 1498 reads: "From here one might send, in the name of the Holy Trinity, as many slaves as could be sold&#160;..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolwing2002_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rolwing2002-87">[83]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columbus was eventually forced to make peace with the rebellious colonists on humiliating terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pickering-3rd_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pickering-3rd-88">[84]</a></sup> In 1500, the Crown had him removed as governor, arrested, and transported in chains to Spain (see <a href="#Accusations_of_tyranny">"Accusations of tyranny"</a> section below). He was eventually freed and allowed to return to the New World, but not as governor.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fourth_voyage">Fourth voyage</span></h3>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Columbus&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.
